<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Airbag</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="hatnote" role="note">This article is about a car safety device. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Airbag_(disambiguation)" title="Airbag (disambiguation)">Airbag (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg/220px-Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg/330px-Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg/440px-Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peugeot_306_airbags_deployed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The driver and passenger front airbag modules, after having been deployed, in a <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_306" title="Peugeot 306">Peugeot 306</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An <b>airbag</b> is a type of <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">vehicle safety</a> device and is an occupant restraint system. The airbag module is designed <b>to inflate extremely rapidly then quickly deflate</b> during a <a href="/wiki/Collision" title="Collision">collision</a> or impact with a surface or a rapid sudden deceleration. It consists of the airbag cushion, a flexible fabric bag, inflation module and impact sensor. The purpose of the airbag is to provide the occupants a soft cushioning and restraint during a crash event to prevent any impact or impact-caused injuries between the flailing occupant and the interior of the vehicle. The airbag provides an energy absorbing surface between the vehicle's occupant and a steering wheel, instrumental panel, A-B-C- structural body frame pillars, headliner and windshield/windscreen.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Description">Description</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Description">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Modern <a href="/wiki/Vehicle" title="Vehicle">vehicles</a> may contain multiple airbag modules in various configurations including:</p>
<ul>
<li>Driver airbag module</li>
<li>Passenger airbag module</li>
<li>Side curtain airbag module</li>
<li>Seat-mounted side impact airbag module</li>
<li>Knee bolster airbag module</li>
<li>Inflatable seat-belt modules</li>
<li>Front Right Side Airbag Sensor</li>
<li>Front Left Side Airbag Sensor</li>
</ul>
<p><br/>
During a crash event, the vehicle's crash sensor(s) provide crucial information to the airbag electronic controller unit (ECU), including collision type, angle and severity of impact. Using this information, the airbag electronic controller unit's crash algorithm determines if the crash event meets the criteria for deployment and triggers various firing circuits to deploy one or more airbag modules within the vehicle. Working as a supplemental restraint system to the vehicle's seat-belt systems, airbag module deployments are triggered through a <a href="/wiki/Pyrotechnics" title="Pyrotechnics">pyrotechnic</a> process that is designed to be used once. Newer side-impact airbag modules consist of compressed air cylinders that are triggered in the event of a side impact vehicle impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first commercial designs were introduced in passenger automobiles during the 1970s with limited success. Broad commercial adoption of airbags occurred in many markets during the late 1980s and early 1990s with a driver airbag, and a front passenger airbag as well on some cars; and many modern vehicles now include six or more units.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Over time, various manufacturers have used different terms for airbags. In the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> marketed its first airbag modules under the unwieldy name "Air Cushion Restraint System (ACRS)". Common terms in North America refer to a nominal role as a supplement to "active" restraints, i.e. seat belts. Because no action by a vehicle occupant is required to activate or use the airbag, it is considered a "passive" device. This is in contrast to <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belts</a>, which are considered "active" devices because the vehicle occupant must act to enable them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>This terminology is not related to <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety#Active_and_passive_safety" title="Automobile safety">active and passive safety</a>, which are, respectively, systems designed to prevent accidents in the first place, and systems designed to minimize the effects of accidents once they occur. In this usage, a car <a href="/wiki/Anti-lock_braking_system" title="Anti-lock braking system">Anti-lock Braking System</a> (ABS) will qualify as an active-safety device, while both its seatbelts and airbags will qualify as passive-safety devices. Further terminological confusion can arise from the fact that passive devices and systems—those requiring no input or action by the vehicle occupant—can operate independently in an active manner; an airbag is one such device. Vehicle safety professionals are generally careful in their use of language to avoid this sort of confusion, though <a href="/wiki/Advertising" title="Advertising">advertising</a> principles sometimes prevent such <a href="/wiki/Semantics" title="Semantics">semantic</a> caution in the consumer marketing of safety features. Further confusing the terminology, the <a href="/wiki/Aviation_safety" title="Aviation safety">aviation safety</a> community uses the terms "active" and "passive" in the <i>opposite</i> sense from the automotive industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>In patent applications, various airbag manufacturers sometimes use the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catchall" title="Catchall">catchall</a> term 'inflatable occupant restraint systems' for vehicle airbags.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1232" data-file-width="1632" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg/220px-Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg/330px-Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg/440px-Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interior_of_1975_Buick_Electra.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1975 <a href="/wiki/Buick_Electra" title="Buick Electra">Buick Electra</a> with ACRS</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The airbag specified for automobile use traces its origins to air-filled bladders as early as 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The invention is also credited independently to the German engineer Walter Linderer, and to the American <a href="/wiki/John_W._Hetrick" title="John W. Hetrick">John W. Hetrick</a> who in 1951 registered for the first of his airbag <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Linderer filed German patent #896,312 on 6 October 1951, which was issued on 12 November 1953, approximately three months after American John Hetrick was issued United States patent #2,649,311 on 18 August 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Linderer's airbag was based on a <a href="/wiki/Compressed_air" title="Compressed air">compressed air</a> system, either released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bumper_(automobile)" title="Bumper (automobile)">bumper</a> contact or by the driver. Later research during the 1960s showed that compressed air could not inflate Linderer's airbag fast enough for maximum safety, thus making it an impractical system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Ideas_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Ideas-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hetrick was an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_engineering" title="Industrial engineering">industrial engineer</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>. His airbag was designed based on his experiences with compressed air from <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedoes</a> during his service in the Navy, combined with a desire to provide protection for his family in their automobile during accidents. Hetrick worked with the major American automobile corporations at the time, but they chose not to invest in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Although airbags are now required in every automobile sold in the United States, Hetrick's 1951 patent filing serves as an example of a "valuable" invention with little economic value to its inventor because its first commercial use did not occur until after the patent expired when in 1971, it was installed as an experiment in a few <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Japan, <a class="extiw" href="https://ja.wikipedia.org/wiki/%E5%B0%8F%E5%A0%80%E4%BF%9D%E4%B8%89%E9%83%8E" title="ja:小堀保三郎">Yasuzaburou Kobori</a> (小堀保三郎) started developing an airbag "safety net" system in 1964, for which he was later awarded patents in 14 countries. He died in 1975 without seeing widespread adoption of airbag systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1967, a breakthrough occurred in the development of airbag crash <a href="/wiki/Sensor" title="Sensor">sensors</a> when Allen K. Breed invented a mechanically-based ball-in-tube component for crash detection, an <a href="/wiki/Electromechanics" title="Electromechanics">electromechanical</a> sensor with a steel ball attached to a tube by a <a href="/wiki/Magnet" title="Magnet">magnet</a> that would inflate an airbag in under 30 milliseconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> A small explosion of <a href="/wiki/Sodium_azide" title="Sodium azide">sodium azide</a> instead of compressed air was used for the first time during inflation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Ideas_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Ideas-13">[13]</a></sup> Breed Corporation then marketed this innovation first to <a href="/wiki/Chrysler" title="Chrysler">Chrysler</a>. A similar "Auto-Ceptor" crash-restraint, developed by the <a href="/wiki/Eaton_Corporation" title="Eaton Corporation">Eaton, Yale &amp; Towne</a> company for Ford was soon offered as an automatic safety system in the United States,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> while the Italian Eaton-Livia company offered a variant with localized<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag needs further explanation. (June 2014)">further explanation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> air cushions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thetimes_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-thetimes-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the early 1970s, Ford and General Motors began offering cars equipped with airbags, initially in government <a href="/wiki/Fleet_vehicle" title="Fleet vehicle">fleet purchased</a> Chevrolet automobiles. GM's <a href="/wiki/Oldsmobile_Toronado" title="Oldsmobile Toronado">Oldsmobile Toronado</a> was the first domestic vehicle to include a passenger airbag.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The automaker discontinued the option for its 1977 <a href="/wiki/Model_year" title="Model year">model year</a>, citing lack of consumer interest. Ford and GM then spent years <a href="/wiki/Lobbying" title="Lobbying">lobbying</a> against air-bag requirements, claiming that the devices were unfeasible and inappropriate. Chrysler made a driver-side airbag standard on 1988–1989 models, but it was not until the early 1990s that airbags became widespread in American cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_supplement_to_seat_belts">As a supplement to seat belts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: As a supplement to seat belts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Airbags for passenger cars were introduced in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> in the mid-1970s, when <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belt</a> usage rates in the country were quite low. Ford built an experimental fleet of cars with airbags in 1971, followed by General Motors in 1973 on Chevrolet vehicles. The early fleet of experimental GM vehicles equipped with airbags experienced seven fatalities, one of which was later suspected to have been caused by the airbag.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1974, GM made its "Air Cushion Restraint System" (ACRS) available as a regular production option (RPO code AR3) in full-size Cadillacs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Buick and Oldsmobile models. The GM cars from the 1970s equipped with ACRS had a driver-side airbag, a driver-side knee restraint<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldcarbrochures1974_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-oldcarbrochures1974-27">[27]</a></sup> (which consists of a padded lower dashboard), and a passenger-side airbag. The passenger-side airbag protects both front passengers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oldcarbrochures1974_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-oldcarbrochures1974-27">[27]</a></sup> and unlike most newer ones, it integrated a knee cushion and a torso cushion, and it also had dual stage deployment which varied depending on the force of the impact. The cars equipped with ACRS had lap belts for all seating positions but they did not have shoulder belts. Shoulder belts were already mandatory equipment in the United States on closed cars without airbags for the driver and outer front passenger seating positions, but GM chose to market its airbags as a substitute for shoulder belts.</p>
<p>The early development of airbags coincided with an international interest in <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">automobile safety</a> legislation. Some safety experts advocated a <a href="/wiki/Risk_assessment" title="Risk assessment">performance-based</a> occupant protection standard rather than a standard mandating a particular technical solution, which could rapidly become outdated and might not be a <a href="/wiki/Cost-effectiveness_analysis" title="Cost-effectiveness analysis">cost-effective</a> approach. Nevertheless, as countries successively mandated seat belt restraints, there was less emphasis placed on other designs for several decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thetimes_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-thetimes-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="As_a_supplemental_restraint_system_.28SRS.29">As a supplemental restraint system (SRS)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: As a supplemental restraint system (SRS)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Frontal_airbag">Frontal airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Frontal airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:453px;max-width:453px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbag1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="619" data-file-width="881" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Airbag1.jpg/150px-Airbag1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Airbag1.jpg/225px-Airbag1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Airbag1.jpg/300px-Airbag1.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:143px;max-width:143px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbag2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="660" data-file-width="881" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Airbag2.jpg/141px-Airbag2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Airbag2.jpg/212px-Airbag2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Airbag2.jpg/282px-Airbag2.jpg 2x" width="141"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbag3.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="615" data-file-width="881" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbag3.jpg/150px-Airbag3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbag3.jpg/225px-Airbag3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Airbag3.jpg/300px-Airbag3.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Three photos of a crash test dummy whose head lands right into the airbag.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The auto industry and research and regulatory communities have moved away from their initial view of the airbag as a seat belt replacement, and the bags are now nominally designated as <b>Supplemental Restraint System (SRS)</b> or Supplemental Inflatable Restraints.</p>
<p>In 1981, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> introduced the airbag in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> as an option on its flagship saloon model, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_W126" title="Mercedes-Benz W126">S-Class (W126)</a>. In the Mercedes system, the sensors would automatically pre-tension the seat belts to reduce occupant's motion on impact (now a common feature), and then deploy the airbag on impact. This integrated the seat belts and airbag into a restraint system, rather than the airbag being considered an alternative to the seat belt.</p>
<p>In 1987, the <a href="/wiki/Porsche_944" title="Porsche 944">Porsche 944</a> Turbo became the first car to have driver and passenger airbags as standard equipment. The less powerful Porsche 944 and 944S had this as an available option. The same year also saw the first airbag in a Japanese car, the <a href="/wiki/Honda_Legend" title="Honda Legend">Honda Legend</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1988, Chrysler was the first United States company to install standard driver's side air bags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Godshall_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Godshall-29">[29]</a></sup> They came in six lines of its high volume production passenger cars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The following year, Chrysler became the first United States auto manufacturer to install driver-side air bags in all its domestic-built automobiles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> All versions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chrysler_S_platform" title="Chrysler S platform">Chrysler minivans</a> came with airbags starting January 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Godshall_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Godshall-29">[29]</a></sup> In 1992, the <a href="/wiki/Jeep_Grand_Cherokee" title="Jeep Grand Cherokee">Jeep Grand Cherokee</a> became the first SUV with airbags in the market place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Driver and passenger air bags became standard equipment in all <a href="/wiki/Dodge_Intrepid" title="Dodge Intrepid">Dodge Intrepid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eagle_Vision" title="Eagle Vision">Eagle Vision</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_Concorde" title="Chrysler Concorde">Chrysler Concorde</a> sedans ahead of any regulations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Early 1993 saw the 4-millionth air bag-equipped Chrysler vehicle roll off the assembly line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In October 1993, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dodge_Ram" title="Dodge Ram">Dodge Rams</a> became the first <a href="/wiki/Pickup_truck" title="Pickup truck">pickup trucks</a> with airbags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first known accident between two airbag-equipped automobiles took place in 1990 in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, USA. A 1989 <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_LeBaron" title="Chrysler LeBaron">Chrysler LeBaron</a> crossed the <a href="/wiki/Road_surface_marking" title="Road surface marking">center line</a> and hit another 1989 Chrysler LeBaron in a <a href="/wiki/Head-on_collision" title="Head-on collision">head-on collision</a>, causing both driver airbags to deploy. The drivers suffered only minor injuries despite extensive damage to the vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>The United States <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_Surface_Transportation_Efficiency_Act" title="Intermodal Surface Transportation Efficiency Act">Intermodal Surface Transportation Efficiency Act</a> of 1991 required passenger cars and light trucks built after 1 September 1998 to have air bags for the driver and the right front passenger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirBagTechnology_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-AirBagTechnology-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> In the United States, NHTSA estimated that air bags had saved over 4,600 lives by 1 September 1999; however, the crash deployment experience of the early 1990s installations indicated that some fatalities and serious injuries were in fact caused by air bags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirBagTechnology_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-AirBagTechnology-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1998, NHTSA initiated new rules for advanced air bags that gave automakers more flexibility in devising effective technological solutions. The revised rules also required improved protection for occupants of different sizes regardless of whether they use seat belts, while minimizing the risk to infants, children, and other occupants caused by air bags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AirBagTechnology_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-AirBagTechnology-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, airbags were almost entirely absent from mainstream cars until the early 1990s. By 1991, four manufacturers - <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a> - offered the air bag on some of their higher-end models, but shortly afterwards, airbags became a common feature on more mainstream cars.</p>
<p>The first European <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford</a> to feature an airbag was the facelifted <a href="/wiki/Ford_Escort_(Europe)" title="Ford Escort (Europe)">Escort Mark V</a> in 1992; within a year, the entire Ford range had at least one airbag as standard. By the mid-1990s, European market leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a>/<a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rover_Group" title="Rover Group">Rover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peugeot" title="Peugeot">Peugeot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiat_S.p.A." title="Fiat S.p.A.">Fiat</a> had included airbags as at least optional equipment across their model ranges. By 1999, it was very rare to find a new mass market car without at least one airbag, and some late 1990s products, such as the <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Golf_Mk4" title="Volkswagen Golf Mk4">Volkswagen Golf Mk4</a>, also featured side airbags. The <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_306" title="Peugeot 306">Peugeot 306</a> is one example of the European automotive mass-market evolution: starting in early 1993, most of these models did not even offer a driver's airbag as an option, but by 1999, even side airbags were available on several variants. On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Audi" title="Audi">Audi</a> was late to offer airbag systems on a broader scale, since even in the 1994 model year its popular models did not offer airbags. Instead, the German automaker until then relied solely on its proprietary cable-based <a href="/wiki/Procon-ten" title="Procon-ten">procon-ten</a> restraint system.</p>
<p>From around the year 2000, side-impact airbags became commonplace on even low- to mid-range vehicles, such as the smaller-engined versions of the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Fiesta" title="Ford Fiesta">Ford Fiesta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_206" title="Peugeot 206">Peugeot 206</a>, and curtain airbags were also becoming regular features on mass-market cars. The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Avensis" title="Toyota Avensis">Toyota Avensis</a>, launched in 2003, was the first mass-market car to be sold in Europe with nine airbags.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adaptive_airbag" title="Adaptive airbag">Variable force deployment</a> front airbags were developed to help minimize injury from the airbag itself.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Shaped_airbags">Shaped airbags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Shaped airbags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C4" title="Citroën C4">Citroën C4</a> provided the first "shaped" driver airbag, made possible by this car's unusual fixed hub steering wheel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Side_airbag">Side airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Side airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1932" data-file-width="2580" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg/220px-Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg/330px-Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg/440px-Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seitenairbag_Porsche.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Side airbag inflated permanently for display purposes</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curtainairbags.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="2160" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Curtainairbags.JPG/220px-Curtainairbags.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Curtainairbags.JPG/330px-Curtainairbags.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Curtainairbags.JPG/440px-Curtainairbags.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Curtainairbags.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Deployed curtain airbag and side torso airbag in a <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C4" title="Citroën C4">Citroën C4</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg/220px-Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg/330px-Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg/440px-Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ford_Mondeon_curtain_airbag_deployed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Deployed curtain airbag in an <a href="/wiki/Opel_Vectra" title="Opel Vectra">Opel Vectra</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are essentially two types of side airbags commonly used today: the side torso airbag and the side curtain airbag.</p>
<p>Most vehicles equipped with side curtain airbags also include side torso airbags. However, some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Cobalt" title="Chevrolet Cobalt">Chevrolet Cobalt</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> 2007-09 model <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Silverado" title="Chevrolet Silverado">Chevrolet Silverado/GMC Sierra</a>, and 2009-12 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dodge_Ram" title="Dodge Ram">Dodge Ram</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> do not feature the side torso airbag.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Side_torso_airbag">Side torso airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Side torso airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Side-impact airbags or side torso airbags (side thorax/abdomen airbags) are a category of airbag usually located in the seat, and inflate between the seat occupant and the door. These airbags are designed to reduce the risk of injury to the pelvic and lower abdomen regions. Some vehicles are now being equipped with different types of designs, to help reduce injury and ejection from the vehicle in rollover crashes. More recent side airbag designs include a two chamber system; a firmer lower chamber for the pelvic region and softer upper chamber for the ribcage.</p>
<p>The Swedish company <a href="/wiki/Autoliv" title="Autoliv">Autoliv AB</a>, was granted a patent on side impact airbags, and they were first offered as an option in 1994<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-volvogroup.com_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-volvogroup.com-44">[44]</a></sup> on the 1995 model year <a href="/wiki/Volvo_850" title="Volvo 850">Volvo 850</a>, and as standard equipment on all Volvo cars made after 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-volvogroup.com_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-volvogroup.com-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some cars, such as the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Polo_Mk5" title="Volkswagen Polo Mk5">Volkswagen Polo Mk.5</a> have combined head and torso side airbags. These are fitted in the backrest of the front seats, and protect the head as well as the torso.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Side_tubular_or_curtain_airbag">Side tubular or curtain airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Side tubular or curtain airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>For 1998, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_E38" title="BMW E38">BMW 7-series</a> and smaller 5-series were fitted with a tubular shaped head side airbags (<b>Inflatable Tubular Structure (ITS)</b>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> the "Head Protection System (HPS)" as standard equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> This airbag was designed to offer head protection in side impact collisions and also maintained inflation for up to seven seconds for rollover protection. However, this tubular shaped airbag design has been quickly replaced by an inflatable 'curtain' airbag.</p>
<p>In May 1998 Toyota began offering a side curtain airbag deploying from the roof on the <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Progr%C3%A8s" title="Toyota Progrès">Progrés</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In 1998 the <a href="/wiki/Volvo_S80" title="Volvo S80">Volvo S80</a> was given roof-mounted curtain airbags to protect both front and rear passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Curtain airbags were then made standard equipment on all new Volvo cars from 2000 except for the first generation <a href="/wiki/Volvo_C70" title="Volvo C70">C70</a> which received an enlarged side torso airbag that also protects the head of front seat occupants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-volvogroup.com_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-volvogroup.com-44">[44]</a></sup> The second generation C70 convertible received the world's first door-mounted side-curtain airbags that deployed upwards.</p>
<p>Roll-sensing side curtain airbags found on vehicles more prone to rollovers such as SUVs and pickups will deploy when a rollover is detected instead of just when an actual collision takes place. Often there is a switch to disable the feature in case the driver wants to take the vehicle offroad.</p>
<p>Curtain airbags have been said to reduce brain injury or fatalities by up to 45% in a side impact with an SUV. These airbags come in various forms (e.g., tubular, curtain, door-mounted) depending on the needs of the application.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Many recent <a href="/wiki/Sport_utility_vehicle" title="Sport utility vehicle">SUVs</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-purpose_vehicle" title="Multi-purpose vehicle">MPVs</a> have a long inflatable curtain airbag that protects all 3 rows of seats.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Knee_airbag">Knee airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Knee airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The second driver's side and separate knee airbag was used in the <a href="/wiki/Kia_Sportage" title="Kia Sportage">Kia Sportage</a> (a <a href="/wiki/South_Korean" title="South Korean">Korean</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SUV" title="SUV">SUV</a> launched in 1995) and has been standard equipment since then. The airbag is located beneath the steering wheel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:V08589P076.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/V08589P076.jpg/220px-V08589P076.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/V08589P076.jpg/330px-V08589P076.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/V08589P076.jpg/440px-V08589P076.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:V08589P076.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Deployed passenger knee airbag in a <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Tundra" title="Toyota Tundra">Toyota Tundra</a> after a frontal collision test, the driver side knee airbag also deployed. Blue and yellow markings indicate the dummy's knees.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Caldina" title="Toyota Caldina">Toyota Caldina</a> introduced the first Driver-side SRS knee airbag on the Japanese market in 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Avensis" title="Toyota Avensis">Toyota Avensis</a> became the first vehicle sold in Europe equipped with a driver's knee airbag.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EuroNCAP" title="EuroNCAP">EuroNCAP</a> reported on the 2003 Avensis, "There has been much effort to protect the driver's knees and legs and a knee airbag worked well."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Since then certain models have also included front passenger knee airbags, which deploy near or over the <a href="/wiki/Glove_compartment" title="Glove compartment">glove compartment</a> in a crash. Knee airbags are designed to reduce leg injury. The knee airbag has become increasingly common from 2000.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rear_curtain_airbag">Rear curtain airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rear curtain airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2008, the new <a href="/wiki/Toyota_iQ" title="Toyota iQ">Toyota iQ</a> microcar featured the first production rear curtain shield airbag to protect the rear occupants' heads in the event of a rear end impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seat_cushion">Seat cushion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Seat cushion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Another feature of the Toyota iQ was a seat cushion airbag in the passenger seat. This is to prevent the pelvis from diving below the lap belt during a frontal impact or submarining. Later Toyota models such as the Yaris added the feature to the driver's seat as well.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Center_airbag">Center airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Center airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:V08232P024.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/V08232P024.jpg/220px-V08232P024.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/V08232P024.jpg/330px-V08232P024.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/V08232P024.jpg/440px-V08232P024.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:V08232P024.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Front-center airbag of a <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Traverse" title="Chevrolet Traverse">Chevrolet Traverse</a> deployed in an static out-of-position test. The purpose of the test was to find out how this airbag affects a 3 year old kid who is out of his seat and in the direct reach of the airbag.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gurtairbag.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1936" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gurtairbag.jpg/170px-Gurtairbag.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gurtairbag.jpg/255px-Gurtairbag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Gurtairbag.jpg/340px-Gurtairbag.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gurtairbag.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seat belt airbag</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2009, Toyota developed the first production rear-seat center airbag designed to reduce the severity of secondary injuries to rear passengers in a side collision. This system deploys from the rear center seat first appearing in on the redesigned <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Crown_Majesta" title="Toyota Crown Majesta">Crown Majesta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In late 2012 General Motors with supplier Takata introduced a front center airbag, it deploys from the driver's seat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 2013 GM Traverse, Acadia, and Enclave will be the first vehicles to use a center airbag for center passengers in the front row.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seat_belt_airbag">Seat belt airbag</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Seat belt airbag">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The seat belt airbag is designed to better distribute the forces experienced by a buckled person in a crash by means of increased seat belt area. This is done to reduce possible injuries to the rib cage or chest of the belt wearer.</p>
<ul>
<li>2009: <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class_(W221)" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class (W221)">Mercedes ESF 2009</a> <a href="/wiki/Experimental_Safety_Vehicle" title="Experimental Safety Vehicle">Experimental Safety Vehicle</a> had seat belt airbags</li>
<li>2010: <a href="/wiki/Lexus_LFA" title="Lexus LFA">Lexus LFA</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> had seat belt airbags for driver and passenger<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li>2011: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Explorer" title="Ford Explorer">Ford Explorer</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbeltairbags_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-fbeltairbags-61">[61]</a></sup> and 2013 <a href="/wiki/Ford_Flex" title="Ford Flex">Ford Flex</a>: optional rear seat belt airbags; standard on the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_MKT" title="Lincoln MKT">Lincoln MKT</a></li>
<li>2013: <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_S-Class_(W222)" title="Mercedes-Benz S-Class (W222)">Mercedes-Benz S-Class (W222)</a> has rear seat <i>beltbags</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li>2014: <a href="/wiki/Ford_Mondeo_(fourth_generation)" title="Ford Mondeo (fourth generation)">Ford Mondeo Mk V</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> has optional rear seat belt airbags for the two outer seats<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cessna_Aircraft" title="Cessna Aircraft">Cessna Aircraft</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> also introduced seat belt airbags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cessnaairbags_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-cessnaairbags-66">[66]</a></sup> They are as of 2003<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cessnaairbags_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-cessnaairbags-66">[66]</a></sup> standard on the 172, 182, and 206.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pedestrian">Pedestrian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Pedestrian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Airbag(s) mounted to the exterior of vehicles, so called <i>pedestrian airbags</i>, are designed to reduce injuries in the event of a vehicle to pedestrian collision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> When a collision is detected the airbag will deploy and cover hard areas, such as a-pillars<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LRDS_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-LRDS-68">[68]</a></sup> and bonnet edges, before they can be struck by the pedestrian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> When introduced in 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Volvo_V40_(P1)" title="Volvo V40 (P1)">Volvo V40</a> included the world's first pedestrian airbag as standard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> As a result, the V40 ranked highest (88%) in the EuroNCAP's pedestrian tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The 2014 Land Rover Discovery was fitted with a pedestrian airbag as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LRDS_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-LRDS-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LRDS60_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-LRDS60-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Manufactures">Manufactures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Manufactures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>SRS airbag suppliers include <a href="/wiki/Autoliv" title="Autoliv">Autoliv</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daicel" title="Daicel">Daicel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Takata_Corporation" title="Takata Corporation">Takata</a> , <a href="/wiki/TRW_Automotive" title="TRW Automotive">TRW</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Key_Safety_Systems&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Key Safety Systems (page does not exist)">KSS</a>, formerly Breed, one of the pioneers in the field.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="On_motorcycles">On motorcycles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: On motorcycles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Motorradairbag.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1870" data-file-width="2520" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Motorradairbag.JPG/220px-Motorradairbag.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Motorradairbag.JPG/330px-Motorradairbag.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Motorradairbag.JPG/440px-Motorradairbag.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Motorradairbag.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Airbag on a motorcycle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Various types of airbags were tested on motorcycles by the UK <a href="/wiki/Transport_Research_Laboratory" title="Transport Research Laboratory">Transport Research Laboratory</a> in the mid-1970s. In 2006 <a href="/wiki/Honda" title="Honda">Honda</a> introduced the first production <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">motorcycle</a> airbag safety system on its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gold_Wing" title="Gold Wing">Gold Wing</a> motorcycle. Honda claims that sensors in the front forks can detect a severe frontal collision and decide when to deploy the airbag, absorbing some of the forward energy of the rider and reducing the velocity at which the rider may be thrown from the motorcycle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Airbag suits have also been developed for use by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorcycle_Grand_Prix" title="Motorcycle Grand Prix">Motorcycle Grand Prix</a> riders. In their earlier form, they were connected to the motorcycle by a cable and deployed when the cable became detached from its mounting clip, inflating to protect the back of the rider. The French manufacturer Helite specializes exclusively in developing airbag jackets for motorcyclists, snowmobile riders and horseback riders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Further developments were conducted by <a href="/wiki/Dainese" title="Dainese">Dainese</a> and led to an autonomous system on board the leathers, without a cable connected to the bike. Instead, an electronic system detects a fall and triggers the inflation of the nitrogen airbags to protect the rider's upper body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation">Operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(May 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1288" data-file-width="1936" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg/220px-2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg/330px-2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg/440px-2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2008-04-14_Airbag_control_unit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An ACU from a <a href="/wiki/Geo_Storm" title="Geo Storm">Geo Storm</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The airbags in the vehicle are controlled by a central Airbag control unit<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> (ACU), a specific type of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_control_unit" title="Electronic control unit">ECU</a>. The ACU monitors a number of related sensors within the vehicle, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accelerometers" title="Accelerometers">accelerometers</a>, impact sensors, side (door) pressure sensors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wheel_speed_sensor" title="Wheel speed sensor">wheel speed sensors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gyroscope" title="Gyroscope">gyroscopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pressure_sensor" title="Pressure sensor">brake pressure sensors</a>, and seat occupancy sensors. The bag itself and its inflation mechanism is concealed within the steering wheel boss (for the driver), or the dashboard (for the front passenger), behind plastic flaps or doors which are designed to "tear open" under the force of the bag inflating. Once the requisite 'threshold' has been reached or exceeded, the airbag control unit will trigger the ignition of a <a href="/wiki/Gas_generator" title="Gas generator">gas generator</a> propellant to rapidly inflate a fabric bag. As the vehicle occupant collides with and squeezes the bag, the gas escapes in a controlled manner through small vent holes. The airbag's volume and the size of the vents in the bag are tailored to each vehicle type, to spread out the deceleration of (and thus force experienced by) the occupant over time and over the occupant's body, compared to a seat belt alone.</p>
<p>The signals from the various sensors are fed into the Airbag control unit, which determines from them the angle of impact, the severity, or force of the crash, along with other variables. Depending on the result of these calculations, the ACU may also deploy various additional restraint devices, such as <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belt</a> pre-tensioners, and/or airbags (including frontal bags for driver and front passenger, along with seat-mounted side bags, and "curtain" airbags which cover the side glass). Each restraint device is typically activated with one or more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyrotechnic" title="Pyrotechnic">pyrotechnic</a> devices, commonly called an initiator or <a href="/wiki/Electric_match" title="Electric match">electric match</a>. The electric match, which consists of an electrical conductor wrapped in a combustible material, activates with a current pulse between 1 and 3 amperes in less than 2 milliseconds. When the conductor becomes hot enough, it ignites the combustible material, which initiates the gas generator. In a seat belt pre-tensioner, this hot gas is used to drive a piston that pulls the slack out of the seat belt. In an airbag, the initiator is used to ignite solid propellant inside the airbag inflator. The burning propellant generates inert gas which rapidly inflates the airbag in approximately 20 to 30 milliseconds. An airbag must inflate quickly in order to be fully inflated by the time the forward-traveling occupant reaches its outer surface. Typically, the decision to deploy an airbag in a frontal crash is made within 15 to 30 milliseconds after the onset of the crash, and both the driver and passenger airbags are fully inflated within approximately 60-80 milliseconds after the first moment of vehicle contact. If an airbag deploys too late or too slowly, the risk of occupant injury from contact with the inflating airbag may increase. Since more distance typically exists between the passenger and the instrument panel, the passenger airbag is larger and requires more gas to fill it.</p>
<p>Older airbag systems contained a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Sodium_azide" title="Sodium azide">sodium azide</a> (NaN<sub>3</sub>), KNO<sub>3</sub>, and SiO<sub>2</sub>. A typical driver-side airbag contains approximately 50-80 g of NaN<sub>3</sub>, with the larger passenger-side airbag containing about 250 g. Within about 40 milliseconds of impact, all these components react in three separate reactions that produce nitrogen gas. The reactions, in order, are as follows.</p>
<p>(1) 2 NaN<sub>3</sub> → 2 Na + 3 N<sub>2</sub> (g)</p>
<p>(2) 10 Na + 2 KNO<sub>3</sub> → K<sub>2</sub>O + 5 Na<sub>2</sub>O + N<sub>2</sub> (g)</p>
<p>(3) K<sub>2</sub>O + Na<sub>2</sub>O + 2 SiO<sub>2</sub> → K<sub>2</sub>SiO<sub>3</sub> + Na<sub>2</sub>SiO<sub>3</sub> (silicate glass)</p>
<p>The first reaction is the decomposition of NaN<sub>3</sub> under high temperature conditions using an electric impulse. This impulse generates to 300 °C temperatures required for the decomposition of the NaN<sub>3</sub> which produces Na metal and N<sub>2</sub> gas. Since Na metal is highly reactive, the KNO<sub>3</sub> and SiO<sub>2</sub> react and remove it, in turn producing more N<sub>2</sub> gas. The second reaction shows just that. The reason that KNO<sub>3</sub> is used rather than something like NaNO<sub>3</sub> is because it is less hygroscopic. It is very important that the materials used in this reaction are not hygroscopic because absorbed moisture can de-sensitize the system and cause the reaction to fail. The final reaction is used to eliminate the K<sub>2</sub>O and Na<sub>2</sub>O produced in the previous reactions because the first-period metal oxides are highly reactive. These products react with SiO<sub>2</sub> to produce a silicate glass which is a harmless and stable compound.</p>
<p>According to a patent<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (August 2015)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup>, the particle size of the sodium azide, potassium nitrate, and silicon dioxide are important. The NaN<sub>3</sub> and KNO<sub>3</sub> must be between 10 and 20 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%9Cm" title="Μm">µm</a>, while the SiO<sub>2</sub> must be between 5 and 10 µm.</p>
<p>There are ongoing efforts to find alternative compounds that can be used in airbags which have less toxic byproducts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In a journal article by Akiyoshi et. Al., it was found that for the reaction of the Sr complex nitrate, (Sr(NH<sub>2</sub>NHCONHNH<sub>2</sub>)∙(NO<sub>3</sub>)<sub>2</sub> of carbohydrazide (SrCDH) with various oxidizing agents resulted in the evolution of N<sub>2</sub> and CO<sub>2</sub> gases. Using KBrO<sub>3</sub> as the oxidizing agent resulted in the most vigorous reaction as well as the lowest initial temperature of reaction. The N<sub>2</sub> and CO<sub>2</sub> gases evolved made up 99% of all gases evolved. Nearly all the starting materials won’t decompose until reaching temperatures of 500 °C or higher so this could be a viable option as an air bag gas generator. In a patent containing another plausible alternative to NaN<sub>3</sub> driven airbags, the gas generating materials involved the use of <a href="/wiki/Guanidine_nitrate" title="Guanidine nitrate">guanidine nitrate</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/5-aminotetrazole" title="5-aminotetrazole">5-aminotetrazole</a>, bitetrazole dehydrate, <a href="/wiki/Nitroimidazole" title="Nitroimidazole">nitroimidazole</a>, and basic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copper_nitrate" title="Copper nitrate">copper nitrate</a>. It was found that these non-azide reagents allowed for a less toxic, lower combustion temperature reaction and more easily disposable air bag inflation system.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Front airbags normally do not protect the occupants during side, rear, or rollover accidents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Since airbags deploy only once and deflate quickly after the initial impact, they will not be beneficial during a subsequent collision. Safety belts help reduce the risk of injury in many types of crashes. They help to properly position occupants to maximize the airbag's benefits and they help restrain occupants during the initial and any following collisions.</p>
<p>In vehicles equipped with a rollover sensing system, accelerometers and gyroscopes are used to sense the onset of a rollover event. If a rollover event is determined to be imminent, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Side_curtain_airbag" title="Side curtain airbag">side-curtain</a> airbags are deployed to help protect the occupant from contact with the side of the vehicle interior, and also to help prevent occupant ejection as the vehicle rolls over.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Triggering_conditions">Triggering conditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Triggering conditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP(HFZ)_05.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG/220px-Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG/330px-Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG/440px-Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP%28HFZ%29_05.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peugeot_206_1999_Hatchback_1.1_TU1JP(HFZ)_05.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Some cars provide the option to turn off airbags.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Airbags are designed to deploy in frontal and near-frontal collisions more severe than a threshold defined by the regulations governing vehicle construction in whatever particular market the vehicle is intended for: United States regulations require deployment in crashes at least equivalent in deceleration to a 23 km/h (14 mph) barrier collision, or similarly, striking a parked car of similar size across the full front of each vehicle at about twice the speed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> International regulations are performance based, rather than technology-based, so airbag deployment threshold is a function of overall vehicle design.</p>
<p>Unlike <a href="/wiki/Crash_test" title="Crash test">crash tests</a> into barriers, real-world crashes typically occur at angles other than directly into the front of the vehicle, and the crash forces usually are not evenly distributed across the front of the vehicle. Consequently, the relative speed between a striking and struck vehicle required to deploy the airbag in a real-world crash can be much higher than an equivalent barrier crash. Because airbag sensors measure deceleration, vehicle speed is not a good indicator of whether an airbag should have deployed. Airbags can deploy due to the vehicle's undercarriage striking a low object protruding above the roadway due to the resulting deceleration.</p>
<p>The airbag sensor is a <a href="/wiki/Microelectromechanical_systems" title="Microelectromechanical systems">MEMS</a> <a href="/wiki/Accelerometer" title="Accelerometer">accelerometer</a>, which is a small <a href="/wiki/Integrated_circuit" title="Integrated circuit">integrated circuit</a> with integrated micro mechanical elements. The microscopic mechanical element moves in response to rapid deceleration, and this motion causes a change in capacitance, which is detected by the electronics on the chip that then sends a signal to fire the airbag. The most common MEMS accelerometer in use is the ADXL-50 by <a href="/wiki/Analog_Devices" title="Analog Devices">Analog Devices</a>, but there are other MEMS manufacturers as well.</p>
<p>Initial attempts using <a href="/wiki/Mercury_switch" title="Mercury switch">mercury switches</a> did not work well. Before MEMS, the primary system used to deploy airbags was called a "<a href="/wiki/Rolamite" title="Rolamite">rolamite</a>". A rolamite is a mechanical device, consisting of a roller suspended within a tensioned band. As a result of the particular geometry and material properties used, the roller is free to translate with little <a href="/wiki/Friction" title="Friction">friction</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hysteresis" title="Hysteresis">hysteresis</a>. This device was developed at <a href="/wiki/Sandia_National_Laboratories" title="Sandia National Laboratories">Sandia National Laboratories</a>. The rolamite, and similar macro-mechanical devices were used in airbags until the mid-1990s when they were universally replaced with MEMS.</p>
<p>Nearly all airbags are designed to automatically deploy in the event of a vehicle fire when temperatures reach 150-200 °C (300-400 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> This safety feature, often termed auto-ignition, helps to ensure that such temperatures do not cause an explosion of the entire airbag module.</p>
<p>Today, airbag triggering <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algorithms" title="Algorithms">algorithms</a> are becoming much more complex. They try to reduce unnecessary deployments and to adapt the deployment speed to the crash conditions. The algorithms are considered valuable <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_property" title="Intellectual property">intellectual property</a>. Experimental algorithms may take into account such factors as the weight of the occupant, the seat location, seatbelt use, and even attempt to determine if a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baby_seat" title="Baby seat">baby seat</a> is present.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflation">Inflation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Inflation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a single <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">source</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Airbag#.23" title="Talk:Airbag">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(May 2016)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>When the frontal airbags are to deploy, a signal is sent to the <a href="/wiki/Gas_generator" title="Gas generator">inflator unit</a> within the airbag control unit. An igniter starts a rapid <a href="/wiki/Chemical_reaction" title="Chemical reaction">chemical reaction</a> generating primarily <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> gas (N<sub>2</sub>) to fill the airbag making it deploy through the module cover. Some airbag technologies use compressed <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Argon" title="Argon">argon</a> gas with a pyrotechnic operated valve ("hybrid gas generator"), while other technologies use various energetic <a href="/wiki/Propellant" title="Propellant">propellants</a>. Although propellants containing the highly toxic <a href="/wiki/Sodium_azide" title="Sodium azide">sodium azide</a> (NaN<sub>3</sub>) were common in early inflator designs, little to no toxic sodium azide has been found on used airbags.</p>
<p>The azide-containing pyrotechnic gas generators contain a substantial amount of the propellant. The driver-side airbag would contain a canister containing about 50 grams of sodium azide. The passenger side container holds about 200 grams of sodium azide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (May 2016)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The alternative propellants may incorporate, for example, a combination of <a href="/wiki/Nitroguanidine" title="Nitroguanidine">nitroguanidine</a>, phase-stabilized <a href="/wiki/Ammonium_nitrate" title="Ammonium nitrate">ammonium nitrate</a> (NH<sub>4</sub>NO<sub>3</sub>) or other nonmetallic oxidizer, and a nitrogen-rich fuel different from azide (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Tetrazole" title="Tetrazole">tetrazoles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triazole" title="Triazole">triazoles</a>, and their salts). The burn rate modifiers in the mixture may be an alkaline metal <a href="/wiki/Nitrate" title="Nitrate">nitrate</a> (NO<sub>3</sub>-) or <a href="/wiki/Nitrite" title="Nitrite">nitrite</a> (NO<sub>2</sub>-), <a href="/wiki/Dicyanamide" title="Dicyanamide">dicyanamide</a> or its salts, <a href="/wiki/Sodium_borohydride" title="Sodium borohydride">sodium borohydride</a> (NaBH<sub>4</sub>), etc. The coolants and <a href="/wiki/Slag" title="Slag">slag</a> formers may be e.g. <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">silica</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alumina" title="Alumina">alumina</a>, glass, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2016)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (May 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> Other alternatives are e.g. <a href="/wiki/Nitrocellulose" title="Nitrocellulose">nitrocellulose</a> based propellants (which have high gas yield but bad storage stability, and their <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_balance" title="Oxygen balance">oxygen balance</a> requires secondary oxidation of the reaction products to avoid buildup of carbon monoxide), or high-oxygen nitrogen-free organic compounds with inorganic oxidizers (e.g., di or tri<a href="/wiki/Carboxylic_acid" title="Carboxylic acid">carboxylic acids</a> with <a href="/wiki/Chlorate" title="Chlorate">chlorates</a> (ClO<sub>3</sub>-) or <a href="/wiki/Perchlorate" title="Perchlorate">perchlorates</a> (ClO<sub>4</sub>-) and eventually metallic oxides; the nitrogen-free formulation avoids formation of toxic <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a>).</p>
<p>From the onset of the crash, the entire deployment and inflation process is about 0.04 seconds. Because vehicles change speed so quickly in a crash, airbags must inflate rapidly to reduce the risk of the occupant hitting the vehicle's interior.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Variable-force_deployment">Variable-force deployment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Variable-force deployment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Advanced airbag technologies are being developed to tailor airbag deployment to the severity of the crash, the size and posture of the vehicle occupant, belt usage, and how close that person is to the actual airbag. Many of these systems use multi-stage inflators that deploy less forcefully in stages in moderate crashes than in very severe crashes. Occupant sensing devices let the airbag control unit know if someone is occupying a seat adjacent to an airbag, the mass/weight of the person, whether a seat belt or child restraint is being used, and whether the person is forward in the seat and close to the airbag. Based on this information and crash severity information, the airbag is deployed at either at a high force level, a less forceful level, or not at all.</p>
<p>Adaptive airbag systems may utilize multi-stage airbags to adjust the pressure within the airbag. The greater the pressure within the airbag, the more force the airbag will exert on the occupants as they come in contact with it. These adjustments allow the system to deploy the airbag with a moderate force for most collisions; reserving the maximum force airbag only for the severest of collisions. Additional sensors to determine the location, weight or relative size of the occupants may also be used. Information regarding the occupants and the severity of the crash are used by the airbag control unit, to determine whether airbags should be suppressed or deployed, and if so, at various output levels.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="509" data-file-width="600" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg/220px-Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg/330px-Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg/440px-Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Airbag_SEAT_Ibiza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Post-deployment view of a <a href="/wiki/SEAT_Ibiza" title="SEAT Ibiza">SEAT Ibiza</a> airbag</div>
</div>
</div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-deployment">Post-deployment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Post-deployment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A chemical reaction produces a burst of nitrogen to inflate the bag. Once an airbag deploys, deflation begins immediately as the gas escapes through vent(s) in the fabric (or, as it's sometimes called, the cushion) and cools. Deployment is frequently accompanied by the release of dust-like particles, and gases in the vehicle's interior (called effluent).
