Most of this dust consists of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cornstarch" title="Cornstarch">cornstarch</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_chalk" title="French chalk">french chalk</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talcum_powder" title="Talcum powder">talcum powder</a>, which are used to lubricate the airbag during deployment.</p>
<p>Newer designs produce effluent primarily consisting of harmless talcum powder/cornstarch and nitrogen gas. In older designs using an azide-based propellant (usually NaN<sub>3</sub>), varying amounts of <a href="/wiki/Sodium_hydroxide" title="Sodium hydroxide">sodium hydroxide</a> nearly always are initially present. In small amounts this chemical can cause minor irritation to the eyes and/or open wounds; however, with exposure to air, it quickly turns into <a href="/wiki/Sodium_bicarbonate" title="Sodium bicarbonate">sodium bicarbonate</a> (baking soda). However, this transformation is not 100% complete, and invariably leaves residual amounts of hydroxide ion from NaOH. Depending on the type of airbag system, <a href="/wiki/Potassium_chloride" title="Potassium chloride">potassium chloride</a> may also be present.</p>
<p>For most people, the only effect the dust may produce is some minor irritation of the throat and eyes. Generally, minor irritations only occur when the occupant remains in the vehicle for many minutes with the windows closed and no ventilation. However, some people with <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a> may develop a potentially lethal asthmatic attack from inhaling the dust.</p>
<p>Because of the airbag exit flap design of the steering wheel boss and dashboard panel, these items are not designed to be recoverable if an airbag deploys, meaning that they have to be replaced if the vehicle has not been <a href="/wiki/Total_loss" title="Total loss">written off</a> in an accident. Moreover, the dust-like particles and gases can cause irreparable cosmetic damage to the dashboard and upholstery, meaning that minor collisions which result in the deployment of airbags can be costly accidents, even if there are no injuries and there is only minor damage to the vehicle structure.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulatory_specifications">Regulatory specifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Regulatory specifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 11 July 1984, the United States government amended <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FMVSS_208" title="FMVSS 208">Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standard 208</a> (FMVSS 208) to require cars produced after 1 April 1989 to be equipped with a passive restraint for the driver. An airbag or a <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belt</a> would meet the requirements of the standard. Airbag introduction was stimulated by the <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> However, airbags were not mandatory on light trucks until 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, FMVSS 208 was amended to require dual front airbags, and reduced-power, second-generation airbags were also mandated. This was due to the injuries caused by first-generation airbags, though FMVSS 208 continues to require that bags be engineered and calibrated to be able to "save" the life of an <i>unbelted</i> 50th-percentile size and weight "male" <a href="/wiki/Crash_test_dummy" title="Crash test dummy">crash test dummy</a>. Technical performance and validation requirements for the inflator assembly used in airbag modules are specified in <a href="/wiki/SAE_International" title="SAE International">SAE</a> USCAR 24-2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_the_United_States">Outside the United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Outside the United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some countries outside North America adhere to internationalized European <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECE_regulations" title="ECE regulations">ECE vehicle and equipment regulations</a> rather than the United States Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standards. ECE airbags are generally smaller and inflate less forcefully than United States airbags, because the ECE specifications are based on <i>belted</i> crash test dummies. In the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and most other developed countries there is no direct legal requirement for new cars to feature airbags. Instead, the <a href="/wiki/Euro_NCAP" title="Euro NCAP">Euro NCAP</a> vehicle <a href="/wiki/Automobile_safety" title="Automobile safety">safety rating</a> encourages manufacturers to take a comprehensive approach to occupant safety; a good rating can only be achieved by combining airbags with other safety features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncap_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncap-89">[89]</a></sup> Thus almost all new cars now come with at least two airbags as standard.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this section <b>may not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">You may <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Airbag" title="Talk:Airbag">talk page</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_wizard" title="Wikipedia:Article wizard">create a new article</a>, as appropriate.</span> <small><i>(September 2008)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Inadvertent airbag deployment while the vehicle is being serviced can result in severe injury, and an improperly installed or defective airbag unit may not operate or perform as intended. Some countries impose restrictions on the sale, transport, handling, and service of airbags and system components. In <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, airbags are regulated as harmful explosives; only <a href="/wiki/Auto_mechanic" title="Auto mechanic">mechanics</a> with special training are allowed to service airbag systems.</p>
<p>Some automakers (such as <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a>) call for the replacement of undeployed airbags after a certain period of time to ensure their reliability in an accident. One example is the 1992 S500, which has an expiry date sticker attached to the door pillar. Some <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0koda_Auto" title="Škoda Auto">Škoda</a> vehicles indicate an expiry date of 14 years from the date of manufacture. In this case, replacement would be uneconomic as the car would have negligible value at 14 years old, far less than the cost of fitting new airbags. <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a>, on the other hand, has stated "airbags do not require replacement during the lifetime of the vehicle," though this cannot be taken as a guarantee on the device.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BohrAAA_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-BohrAAA-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Limitations">Limitations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Limitations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2160" data-file-width="3840" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG/220px-Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG/330px-Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG/440px-Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Underride_guard_full-width_impact_test.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Crash_test" title="Crash test">Crash test</a> of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Underride_guard" title="Underride guard">underride guard</a> at 30–40 km/h (19–25 mph); the truck platform at head height has been prevented from impacting the <a href="/wiki/Windshield" title="Windshield">windshield</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although the millions of installed airbags in use have an excellent safety record, there are some limitations on their ability to protect car occupants.</p>
<p>The original implementation of front airbags did little to protect against <a href="/wiki/Side_collision" title="Side collision">side collisions</a>, which can be more dangerous than frontal collisions because the protective <a href="/wiki/Crumple_zone" title="Crumple zone">crumple zone</a> in front of the passenger compartment is completely bypassed. Side airbags and protective airbag curtains are increasingly being required in modern vehicles to protect against this very common category of collisions.</p>
<p>Airbags are designed to deploy once only, and are ineffective if there are any further collisions after an initial impact. Multiple impacts may occur during certain rollover accidents or other incidents involving multiple collisions, such as many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-vehicle_collision" title="Multi-vehicle collision">multi-vehicle collisions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hyundai_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>An extremely dangerous situation occurs during "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Underride_collision" title="Underride collision">underride collisions</a>", in which a passenger vehicle collides with the rear of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tractor-trailer" title="Tractor-trailer">tractor-trailer</a> lacking a rear underride guard, or hits the side of such a trailer not equipped with a side underride guard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Underride_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Underride-92">[92]</a></sup> The platform bed of a typical trailer is approximately at the head height of a seated adult occupant of a typical passenger car. This means that there may not be much between a head and the edge of the trailer platform, except a glass <a href="/wiki/Windshield" title="Windshield">windshield</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> In an underride collision, the car's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crush_zone" title="Crush zone">crush zones</a> designed to absorb collision energy are completely bypassed, and the airbags may not deploy in time because the car does not decelerate appreciably until the windshield and roof pillars have already impacted the trailer bed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hyundai_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hyundai-91">[91]</a></sup> Even delayed inflation of airbags may be useless because of major intrusion into the passenger space, leaving occupants at high risk of major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Head_trauma" title="Head trauma">head trauma</a> or <a href="/wiki/Decapitation" title="Decapitation">decapitation</a> in even low speed collisions. Western European standards for underride guards have been stricter than North American standards, which typically have allowed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grandfathering" title="Grandfathering">grandfathering</a> of older equipment that may still be on the road for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Underride_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-Underride-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Typical airbag systems are completely disabled by turning off the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignition_key" title="Ignition key">ignition key</a>. Unexpected turnoffs usually also disable the engine, <a href="/wiki/Power_steering" title="Power steering">power steering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Power_brakes" title="Power brakes">power brakes</a>, and may be the direct cause of an accident. If a violent collision occurs, the disabled airbags will not deploy to protect vehicle occupants. In 2014, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_General_Motors_recall" title="2014 General Motors recall">General Motors admitted to concealing information</a> about fatal accidents caused by defective ignition switches which would abruptly shut down a car (including its airbags). Between 13 and 74 deaths have been directly attributed to this defect, depending on how the fatalities are classified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Injuries_and_fatalities">Injuries and fatalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Injuries and fatalities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags,_NHTSA,_DOT.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="760" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg/220px-Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg/330px-Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg/440px-Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags%2C_NHTSA%2C_DOT.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lives_Saved_by_Safety_Belts_and_Air_Bags,_NHTSA,_DOT.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lives saved by <a href="/wiki/Seat_belt" title="Seat belt">seat belts</a> and airbags in the United States of America over a 10-year period.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Under some rare conditions, airbags can injure and in some very rare instances kill vehicle occupants. To provide crash protection for occupants not wearing seat belts, United States airbag designs trigger much more forcefully than airbags designed to the international ECE standards used in most other countries. Recent "smart" airbag controllers can recognize if a seatbelt is used, and alter the airbag cushion deployment parameters accordingly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1990, the first automotive fatality attributed to an airbag was reported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHTSAAirBag_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-NHTSAAirBag-97">[97]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TRW_Inc." title="TRW Inc.">TRW</a> produced the first gas-inflated airbag in 1994, with sensors and low-inflation-force bags becoming common soon afterwards. Dual-depth (also known as dual-stage) airbags appeared on passenger cars in 1998. By 2005, deaths related to airbags had declined, with no adult deaths and two child deaths attributed to airbags that year. however, injuries remain fairly common in accidents with an airbag deployment.</p>
<p>Serious injuries are less common, but severe or fatal injuries can occur to vehicle occupants very near an airbag or in direct contact when it deploys. Such injuries may be sustained by unconscious drivers slumped over the steering wheel, unrestrained or improperly restrained occupants who slide forward in the seat during pre-crash braking, and properly belted drivers sitting very close to the steering wheel. A good reason for the driver not to cross hands over the steering wheel, a rule taught to most learner drivers but quickly forgotten by most, is that an airbag deployment while negotiating a turn may result in the driver's hand(s) being driven forcefully into his or her face, exacerbating any injuries from the airbag alone.</p>
<p>Improvements in sensing and gas generator technology have allowed the development of third generation airbag systems that can adjust their deployment parameters to size, weight, position and restraint status of the occupant. These improvements have demonstrated a reduced injury risk factor for small adults and children, who had an increased risk of injury with first generation airbag systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>One model of airbags made by the <a href="/wiki/Takata_Corporation" title="Takata Corporation">Takata Corporation</a> used <a href="/wiki/Ammonium_nitrate" title="Ammonium nitrate">ammonium nitrate</a>-based gas generating compositions in airbag inflators instead of the more stable, but more expensive compound <a href="/wiki/Tetrazole" title="Tetrazole">Tetrazole</a>. The ammonium nitrate-based inflators had a flaw where old inflators with long-term exposure to hot and humid climate conditions could rupture during deployment, projecting metal shards though the airbag and into the driver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The defect caused seven deaths and over 100 injuries in the U.S., and one death in Malaysia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> recalled over 33 million vehicles in May 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and fined Takata $70 million in November 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Toyota, Mazda and Honda have said that they will not use ammonium nitrate inflators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbag_fatality_statistics">Airbag fatality statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Airbag fatality statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From 1990 to 2000, the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">National Highway Traffic Safety Administration</a> identified 175 fatalities caused by air bags. Most of these (104) have been children, while the rest were adults. About 3.3 million air bag deployments have occurred during that interval, and the agency estimates more than 6,377 lives saved and countless injuries prevented.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHTSAAirBag_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-NHTSAAirBag-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BohrAAA2_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-BohrAAA2-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>A rear-facing infant restraint put in the front seat of a vehicle places an infant's head close to the airbag, which can cause severe <a href="/wiki/Head_injury" title="Head injury">head injuries</a>, or death if the airbag deploys. Some modern cars include a switch to disable the front passenger airbag, in case a child-supporting seat is used there (although not in Australia, where rear-facing child seats are prohibited in the front where an airbag is fitted).</p>
<p>In vehicles with side airbags, it is dangerous for occupants to lean against the windows, doors, and pillars, or to place objects between themselves and the side of the vehicle. Articles hung from a vehicle's clothes hanger hooks can be hazardous if the vehicle's side curtain airbags deploy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> A seat-mounted airbag may also cause internal injury if the occupant leans against the door.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aerospace_and_military_applications">Aerospace and military applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Aerospace and military applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2036" data-file-width="3060" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg/220px-Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg/330px-Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg/440px-Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pathfinder_Air_Bags_-_GPN-2000-000484.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
NASA engineers test the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Pathfinder" title="Mars Pathfinder">Mars Pathfinder</a> airbag <a href="/wiki/Landing" title="Landing">landing</a> system on simulated Martian terrain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a> industry and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">United States government</a> have applied airbag technologies for many years. <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> have incorporated airbag systems in various aircraft and spacecraft applications as early as the 1960s.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OH-58D_Cockpit_Air_Bag_System_(CABS).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="218" data-file-width="314" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/OH-58D_Cockpit_Air_Bag_System_%28CABS%29.jpg/220px-OH-58D_Cockpit_Air_Bag_System_%28CABS%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/OH-58D_Cockpit_Air_Bag_System_%28CABS%29.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OH-58D_Cockpit_Air_Bag_System_(CABS).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
OH-58D CABS test</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airbag_landing_systems">Airbag landing systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airbag landing systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first use of airbags for <a href="/wiki/Landing" title="Landing">landing</a> were <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">Luna 9</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luna_13" title="Luna 13">Luna 13</a>, which landed on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a> in 1966 and returned panoramic images. The <a href="/wiki/Mars_Pathfinder" title="Mars Pathfinder">Mars Pathfinder</a> lander employed an innovative airbag landing system, supplemented with <a href="/wiki/Aerobraking" title="Aerobraking">aerobraking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parachute" title="Parachute">parachute</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solid_rocket" title="Solid rocket">solid rocket</a> landing thrusters. This prototype successfully tested the concept, and the two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover_Mission" title="Mars Exploration Rover Mission">Mars Exploration Rover Mission</a> landers employed similar landing systems. The <a href="/wiki/Beagle_2" title="Beagle 2">Beagle 2</a> Mars lander also tried to use airbags for landing, the landing was successful and the lander touched down safely, but several of the spacecraft's solar panels failed to deploy, thereby disabling the spacecraft.</p>
<p>Airbags have also been used on military fixed wing aircraft, such as the <a href="/wiki/Escape_crew_capsule#Design_and_development" title="Escape crew capsule">Escape Crew Capsule</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-111_Aardvark" title="F-111 Aardvark">F-111 Aardvark</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Occupant_protection">Occupant protection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbag&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Occupant protection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> has incorporated airbags in its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UH-60_Black_Hawk" title="UH-60 Black Hawk">UH-60A/L</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Black Hawk and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OH-58_Kiowa" title="OH-58 Kiowa">OH-58D</a> Kiowa Warrior<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> helicopter fleets. The Cockpit Air Bag System (CABS)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> consists of forward and lateral airbags, and an inflatable tubular structure (on the OH-58D only) with an Electronic Crash Sensor Unit (ECSU). The CABS system was developed by the United States Army <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Applied_Technology_Directorate" title="Aviation Applied Technology Directorate">Aviation Applied Technology Directorate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Eustis" title="Fort Eustis">Fort Eustis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Va</a> through a contract with Simula Safety Systems (now <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> It is the first conventional airbag system for occupant injury prevention (worldwide) designed and developed and placed in service for an aircraft, and the first specifically for helicopter applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
